# Error Analysis and Resolution

## Error 1: `blockMesh` — Block hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11) is inside-out

The primary error is that the first hex block definition is **inside-out**. Looking at the vertex coordinates:

- **Vertices 0-3**: (-50, 25, 25), (-50, 25, -25), (-50, -25, -25), (-50, -25, 25) — these form the **inlet face** (x = -50)
- **Vertices 8-11**: (-50, 25, 25), (-50, 25, -25), (-50, -25, -25), (-50, -25, 25) — these are **identical** to vertices 0-3

This means the hex block `(0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)` has all 8 vertices lying on the **same plane** (x = -50), which makes it degenerate and inside-out. A hex block requires vertices to span a 3D volume, not be coplanar.

### Proposed Fix

The blockMeshDict needs to be completely reworked to define a proper 3D square bend geometry with four distinct blocks that actually form a volume. The current vertex layout is fundamentally flawed — vertices 0-3 and 8-11 are duplicates, and the block definitions reference vertices that don't form proper hexahedral volumes.

**Key changes needed:**

1. **Redefine vertices** so that each block spans a true 3D region. The square bend tutorial typically uses a structure where:
   - Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to some intermediate x, e.g., -25)
   - Block 1: bend section (curved transition from x-direction to y-direction)
   - Block 2: outlet straight section (y from intermediate y to -50)
   - Block 3: continuation/extension

2. **Fix the block definitions** to use proper vertex indices that form valid hexahedra. Each hex block must have 8 distinct vertices that are not coplanar.

3. **Update boundary faces** to reference the correct vertex indices from the new vertex list.

4. **Remove duplicate vertices** — vertices 0/8, 1/9, 2/10, 3/11 should not be identical.

## Error 2: `p` boundary condition — patch name mismatch

The `0/p` file references boundary patches named `innerWall`, `outerWall`, `lowerWall`, and `upperWall`, but the `blockMeshDict` defines patches named `inlet`, `outlet`, `upperWall`, `lowerWall`, `leftWall`, and `rightWall`. The solver cannot find the `innerWall` and `outerWall` patches.

### Proposed Fix

In the `0/p` file, change the boundary condition entries from `innerWall`/`outerWall` to match the patch names defined in `blockMeshDict`:

- Replace `innerWall` → `leftWall`
- Replace `outerWall` → `rightWall`

So the `p` file's boundary section should have:

```
leftWall
{
    type            zeroGradient;
}
rightWall
{
    type            zeroGradient;
}
```

(And keep `inlet` and `outlet` as they are.)

## Summary of Required Changes

1. **`system/blockMeshDict`**: Completely restructure the vertices and blocks to define a proper 3D square bend with four non-degenerate hex blocks. The current vertex layout with duplicate points and the block `(0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)` being inside-out must be fixed.

2. **`0/p`**: Change `innerWall` → `leftWall` and `outerWall` → `rightWall` to match the patch names in `blockMeshDict`.

These are structural fixes to the mesh definition and boundary condition naming — the mesh must be regenerated with `blockMesh` after making these changes.

# Error Analysis and Resolution

## Error 1: `blockMesh` — Wrong token type (comma expected, found comma)

Looking at the error message: `wrong token type - expected word, found on line 72 the punctuation token ','`

This means that on line 72 of `blockMeshDict`, there is a comma where a **word** is expected. Looking at the `blockMeshDict` content, line 72 is the closing parenthesis of the third block definition:

```
hex (16 17 18 19 20 21 22 23) (100 10 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
```

The issue is that the `simpleGrading` keyword is written as `(1 1 1)` — this is a **list of three numbers**, not a single word. The `blockMesh` parser expects `simpleGrading` to be a **single word** (like `uniform`), not a list in parentheses.

### Proposed Fix

In the `blockMeshDict`, change the `simpleGrading` entries from parenthesized lists to the keyword `uniform`:

- Change `simpleGrading (1 1 1)` → `simpleGrading uniform`
- Change `simpleGrading (100 10 1)` → `simpleGrading uniform`

This is consistent with how the squareBend tutorial defines blocks — `simpleGrading` should be a single word, not a list.

## Error 2: `blockMesh` — Block hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11) is inside-out

This is the same fundamental mesh issue from Attempt 1. The vertices 0-3 and 8-11 are duplicates (both at x = -50), making the first block degenerate and inside-out. The `simpleGrading uniform` fix won't resolve this — the mesh topology itself is wrong.

### Proposed Fix

The vertex layout and block definitions need to be completely restructured to form a proper 3D square bend with four non-degenerate hex blocks. The current approach of duplicating vertices (0=8, 1=9, 2=10, 3=11) creates degenerate blocks.

**Key changes needed:**

1. **Redefine vertices** so that each block spans a true 3D volume. The square bend tutorial typically uses a structure where:
   - Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to some intermediate x, e.g., -25)
   - Block 1: bend section (curved transition from x-direction to y-direction)
   - Block 2: outlet straight section (y from intermediate y to -50)
   - Block 3: continuation/extension

2. **Fix the block definitions** to use proper vertex indices that form valid hexahedra. Each hex block must have 8 distinct vertices that are not coplanar.

3. **Update boundary faces** to reference the correct vertex indices from the new vertex list.

The current vertex numbering approach with duplicate points (0/8, 1/9, 2/10, 3/11) is fundamentally flawed. The vertex list should have 24 unique vertices (8 per block), not 16 with duplicates.

## Error 3: `p` boundary condition — Patch name mismatch

The `0/p` file references `innerWall` and `outerWall`, but the `blockMeshDict` defines `leftWall` and `rightWall`. This was fixed in Attempt 1, but if the vertex/block structure was changed, the patch names might have changed again.

### Proposed Fix

Ensure that the `0/p` file has boundary conditions for `inlet`, `outlet`, `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, and `upperWall` — matching exactly the patch names defined in `blockMeshDict`.

## Summary of Required Changes

1. **`system/blockMeshDict`**: Completely restructure the vertex list and block definitions to create a proper 3D square bend with four non-degenerate hex blocks. The current approach with duplicate vertices (0=8, 1=9, 2=10, 3=11) creates degenerate blocks. The vertex list must have 24 unique vertices, and the block definitions must reference these properly to form valid hexahedra.

2. **`system/blockMeshDict`**: Change `simpleGrading (1 1 1)` and `simpleGrading (100 10 1)` to `simpleGrading uniform` on line 72 and the corresponding line for block 2.

3. **`0/p`**: Ensure boundary condition patch names (`inlet`, `outlet`, `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `upperWall`) match exactly those defined in `blockMeshDict`.

# Error Analysis and Resolution

## Error 1: `blockMesh` — Incorrect first token, expected `<int>` or `'('`, found `uniform,`

Looking at the error: `incorrect first token, expected <int> or '(', found on line 90 the word 'uniform,'`

Line 90 of `blockMeshDict` is the closing parenthesis of the third block definition. The error is that the parser is reading `uniform,` (with a comma) as the first token instead of recognizing the block definition properly. This suggests there's a **syntax error in the block definition format**.

Looking at the current `blockMeshDict`, the blocks are defined as:

```
hex (0 1 2 3 4 5 6 7) (10 10 1) simpleGrading uniform,
hex (8 9 10 11 12 13 14 15) (10 10 1) simpleGrading uniform,
hex (16 17 18 19 20 21 22 23) (100 10 1) simpleGrading uniform,
hex (24 25 26 27 28 29 30 31) (10 10 1) simpleGrading uniform
```

The issue is that **each block definition ends with a comma**, including the last one. In OpenFOAM's `blockMeshDict`, the last block should **not** end with a comma — only the first N-1 blocks should have commas. The comma after the last block confuses the parser.

### Proposed Fix

Remove the comma after the last block definition in `system/blockMeshDict`:

Change:
```
hex (24 25 26 27 28 29 30 31) (10 10 1) simpleGrading uniform,
```

To:
```
hex (24 25 26 27 28 29 30 31) (10 10 1) simpleGrading uniform
```

## Error 2: `blockMesh` — Block hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11) is inside-out

This is the same fundamental mesh topology issue from previous attempts. The vertices 0-3 and 8-11 are duplicates (both at x = -50), making the first block degenerate and inside-out. The `simpleGrading uniform` fix from previous attempts doesn't resolve this — the mesh structure itself is wrong.

### Proposed Fix

The vertex layout and block definitions need to be completely restructured to form a proper 3D square bend with four non-degenerate hex blocks. The current approach with duplicate vertices (0=8, 1=9, 2=10, 3=11) creates degenerate blocks.

**Key changes needed:**

1. **Redefine vertices** so that each block spans a true 3D volume. The square bend tutorial typically uses a structure where:
   - Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to some intermediate x, e.g., -25)
   - Block 1: bend section (curved transition from x-direction to y-direction)
   - Block 2: outlet straight section (y from intermediate y to -50)
   - Block 3: continuation/extension

2. **Fix the block definitions** to use proper vertex indices that form valid hexahedra. Each hex block must have 8 distinct vertices that are not coplanar.

3. **Update boundary faces** to reference the correct vertex indices from the new vertex list.

The current vertex numbering approach with duplicate points (0/8, 1/9, 2/10, 3/11) is fundamentally flawed. The vertex list should have 24 unique vertices (8 per block), not 16 with duplicates.

## Error 3: `p` boundary condition — Patch name mismatch

The `0/p` file references `innerWall` and `outerWall`, but the `blockMeshDict` defines `leftWall` and `rightWall`. This was fixed in previous attempts, but if the vertex/block structure was changed, the patch names might have changed again.

### Proposed Fix

Ensure that the `0/p` file has boundary conditions for `inlet`, `outlet`, `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, and `upperWall` — matching exactly those defined in `blockMeshDict`.

## Summary of Required Changes

1. **`system/blockMeshDict`**: Remove the comma after the last block definition (line 90) — change `uniform,` to `uniform`.

2. **`system/blockMeshDict`**: Completely restructure the vertex list and block definitions to create a proper 3D square bend with four non-degenerate hex blocks. The current approach with duplicate vertices (0=8, 1=9, 2=10, 3=11) creates degenerate blocks. The vertex list must have 24 unique vertices, and the block definitions must reference these properly to form valid hexahedra.

3. **`0/p`**: Ensure boundary condition patch names (`inlet`, `outlet`, `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `upperWall`) match exactly those defined in `blockMeshDict`.

# Error Analysis and Resolution

## Error 1: `blockMesh` — Block hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11) is inside-out

This is the **same fundamental mesh topology issue** that has persisted across all 3 attempts. The vertices 0-3 and 8-11 are duplicates (both at x = -50), making the first block degenerate and inside-out. The `simpleGrading uniform` fix from previous attempts doesn't resolve this — the mesh structure itself is wrong.

## Error 2: `blockMesh` — Incorrect first token, expected `<int>` or `'('`, found `uniform,`

This is the same comma-after-last-block issue from Attempt 3. The last block definition ends with a comma, which confuses the parser.

## Error 3: `rhoSimpleFoam` — Cannot find file "points"

This is a cascading error — since `blockMesh` fails, no mesh is generated, so the solver can't find the mesh files.

## Summary of Required Changes

### 1. `system/blockMeshDict` — Fix the comma issue
Remove the comma after the last block definition (line 90):
- Change `hex (24 25 26 27 28 29 30 31) (10 10 1) simpleGrading uniform,` 
- To `hex (24 25 26 27 28 29 30 31) (10 10 1) simpleGrading uniform`

### 2. `system/blockMeshDict` — **Completely restructure the vertex layout and block definitions** to create a proper 3D square bend with four non-degenerate hex blocks. The current approach with duplicate vertices (0=8, 1=9, 2=10, 3=11) creates degenerate blocks. The vertex list must have 24 unique vertices (8 per block), not 16 with duplicates.

The current vertex numbering approach is fundamentally flawed. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where each block spans a true 3D volume. The vertices should be arranged so that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25)
- Block 1: bend section (curved transition from x-direction to y-direction)  
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75)
- Block 3: extension section (x from -500 to -550)

Each block must have 8 distinct, non-coplanar vertices.

### 3. `0/p` — Ensure boundary patch names match `blockMeshDict`
The `0/p` file references `innerWall` and `outerWall`, but the `blockMeshDict` defines `leftWall` and `rightWall`. These need to be renamed to match exactly.

## Proposed Fix — Vertex and Block Redesign

The current vertex layout with duplicate points (0/8, 1/9, 2/10, 3/11) is the root cause. Here's the correct approach:

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial typically uses a structure where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to some intermediate x, e.g., -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from intermediate y to -50, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.

**Redefine vertices** so that each block has 8 unique, non-coplanar vertices. The square bend tutorial uses a proper 3D topology where the bend is handled by a single block with a curved face, or by carefully arranging vertices so that adjacent blocks share proper faces.

One working approach (as seen in the squareBend tutorial) is to define vertices such that:
- Block 0: inlet straight section (x from -50 to -25, full y/z range)
- Block 1: bend section (transition from x-direction to y-direction, with vertices arranged to form a proper 90° turn)
- Block 2: outlet straight section (y from -50 to -75, full x/z range)
- Block 3: continuation/extension

The key is that **no two blocks should share identical vertex coordinates** — each vertex must be unique and positioned to form a valid 3D hexahedron with its neighboring vertices.

**Specifically, the current vertex numbering must be changed** so that vertices 0-3 are the inlet face (x=-50), vertices 4-7 are the front face of block 0, vertices 8-11 are the back face of block 1 (the bend), vertices 12-15 are the front face of block 1, vertices 16-19 are the back face of block 2 (outlet), and vertices 20-23 are the front face of block 2. There should be **no duplicate coordinates** between blocks.
